## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (nonlinear) second-order oscillators. Common models combine a restoring force term (often nonlinear in x), damping (often dependent on v and sometimes x), and optional external/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring force): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude linear oscillations about equilibrium)
- Damped harmonic oscillator (linear viscous damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper dynamics)
- Driven damped oscillator (external periodic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (forced vibration / resonance)
- Constant-bias forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (gravity/bias or actuator offset shifting equilibrium)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (stronger nonlinear stiffness at large amplitude)
- Pendulum-like restoring torque: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (rotational oscillator where x behaves like an angle)
- Quadratic/nonlinear damping (aerodynamic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared dissipation)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * Sign(v) (sliding friction causing stick-slip tendencies)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent negative damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent negative damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (another canonical self-excited oscillator form)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear restoring saturation (bounded stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x / (c1 + x**2) - c2 * v (restoring force that weakens/saturates at large |x|)
- Amplitude-dependent damping (x-modulated dissipation): dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (damping increases with displacement/strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (and is odd in x); lack of v-dependence suggests near energy conservation.
- Viscous damping signature: a term proportional to -v produces monotonic energy decay; linear -c*v yields exponential decay of amplitude in the linear regime.
- Dry friction signature: Sign(v) or very steep tanh(c*v) approximations create non-smooth dynamics, possible sticking, and nearly constant deceleration magnitude.
- Aerodynamic/drag signature: v*Abs(v) (or v**3) indicates dissipation growing rapidly with speed, leading to faster decay at high amplitudes.
- Nonlinear stiffness signature: odd powers of x (x**3, x**5) indicate hardening/softening; they produce amplitude-dependent frequency shifts.
- Pendulum/rotation signature: sin(c*x) restoring force implies periodic potential and strong nonlinearity at larger angles (departure from linear -x).
- Self-excited/limit-cycle signature: a damping factor that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c - x**2)*v or v - v**3, yields growth at small amplitude and saturation at large amplitude.
- External forcing signature: explicit time dependence like sin(c*t) introduces entrainment and resonance peaks; phase-dependent responses are expected.
- Parametric excitation signature: coefficients multiplying x (or v) that vary with t (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x) create instability tongues and subharmonic responses.
- Equilibrium shift signature: constant (or slowly varying) additive terms in dv_dt move the equilibrium away from x=0, changing the mean position around which oscillations occur.
